العرش ، يسبحون بحمد ربهم ) (۱) وإذا عرفت هذا البحث في الفلك الأعظم ، فاعرف مثله في سائر الأفلاك .
ثم إن أصحاب الطلمسات: أثبتوا لكل درجة من الدرجات الثلاثمائة والستين .. روحاً، يختص بها، إلا أن أثر ذلك الروح إنما(٢) يقوى ويظهر ، عند نزول الشمس في تلك الدرجة، وأثبتوا أيضاً : أرواحاً تدبر الأيام وأرواحاً أخرى تدبر الساعات. وأثبتوا لكل واحد منها نوعاً من التأثيرات وأيضاً : إن كرة الأرض مقسومة بأربعة أقسام : البحار ، والجبال ، والمفاوز ، والعمرانات . وزعموا : أن المدبر لكل واحد من هذه الأقسام : روح من الأرواح [ الفلكية (۳) ] ثم زعموا : أن لكل واحد من البحار مديراً على حدة . وكذا القول في الجبال والمفاوز. وكذا القول أيضاً في البلاد . فإنهم زعموا : أن لكل واحد منها مديراً خاصاً من الأرواح الفلكية . وزعموا : أن للنبات مديراً ، وللطير مديراً ، وللحشرات مديراً ، وكذا القول في السباع وفي البهائم . وهؤلاء رعموا : أن الملل والأديان دالة على هذا المعنى . ألا ترى في لسان صاحب الشريعة عليه السلام ، أنه قال : ( جبريل صاحب الوحي والعلم ، وميكائيل صاحب الأرزاق ، وعزرائيل ملك الموت ) ( وملك الجبال فلان ، وملك البحار فلان. ثم إن أصحاب الطلسمات زعموا : أن الواجب على الإنسان أن يشتغل بطاعة ذلك الروح ، وبعباداته ، وأن يتخذ له هيكلا ، ويشتغل بعبادته . ورأيت أكثر أهل الهند مطبقين على هذا المذهب.
ويليق بهذا الموضع : أن نشرح مذاهب عبدة الأصنام . فنقول : إن العلم الضروري حاصل بأن الحجر المنحوت ، والخشب المنحوت : لا يصلح لإلهية العالم . وما كان معلوم الفساد بالبديهة (1) امتنع إطباق الجمع العظيم عليه زماناً طويلاً ودهراً مديداً . وعبادة الأصنام كانت موجودة قبل مجيء نوح عليه السلام . بدليل : أنه تعالى حكى عن كفار زمانه قولهم : ( لا تذرن آلهتكم . ولا تذرن وداً ، ولا سواعاً ، ولا يغوث ، ويعوق ، ونسرا (۱) ) .
ثم إن ذلك الدين بقي من ذلك الوقت مستمراً في أكثر أطراف الأرض ، إلى هذا الزمان . وذلك يدل على أنه ليس مرادهم منه : اعتقادهم في أن مبر العالم : هو ذلك الخشب والحجر والصورة المفرغة في القالب ، بل لهم فيه تأويلات .
التأويل الأول : الأعظم الأقوى - أن المنجمين وأصحاب الأحكام : زعموا أن المدبر لهذا العالم : هو الكواكب السبعة السيارة . لأجل أنهم شاهدوا أحوال هذا العالم مرتبطة باختلاف أحوال الشمس والقمر . فاعتقدوا إلهية هذه الكواكب . ثم إنها تغيب عن العيون تارة لأجل غروبها ، وتارة لأجل أن الغيم يحجب عن رؤيتها ، وتارة لأجل أن سائر الكواكب تختفي ، بسبب وقوعها (٢) في شعاع الشمس . فلأجل هذا السبب اتخذوا أصناماً على صور تلك الكواكب ، وزينوها بالأشياء المناسبة لتلك الكواكب ثم واظبوا على عبادتها . فهذا هو السبب الأعظم للاشتغال بعبادة الأصنام. ومما يدل عليه : أنه تعالى لما حكى عن الخليل عليه السلام ، أن قال لأبيه آخر : أتتخذ أصناماً آلهة ؟ إني أراك وقومك في ضلاك مبين (٣) . ثم إنه بعد ذكر هذا الكلام : اشتغل بإقامة الدلالة على أن لا يجوز اتخاذ الكواكب والقمر والشمس آلهة . وذلك من أصدق الدلائل الدالة على أن دين عبدة الأوثان : فرع هذا المذهب
التأويل الثاني : ما نقلنا عن الهند وغيرهم. أنهم قالوا : ثبت بالاستقراء وبالوحي أن لكل طرف من أطراف الأرض ولكل طائفة من طوائف الناس : روح فلكي ، يدبرهم ، ويعتني بإصلاح أحوالهم . وإذا كان الأمر كذلك كان
The Throne, they exalt [Him] with praise of their Lord (1). And if you have understood this research concerning the greatest sphere, then know the like regarding the remaining spheres. Then the practitioners of talismans affirmed for each of the three hundred and sixty degrees a spirit specifically associated with it, except that the effect of that spirit only (2) strengthens and appears when the sun descends into that degree. And they also affirmed spirits that manage the days and other spirits that manage the hours. And they affirmed for each of them a kind of influence. Also: the sphere of the earth is divided into four divisions: seas, mountains, deserts, and inhabited areas. And they claimed that the manager of each of these divisions is a spirit from the [celestial] spirits (3). Then they claimed that each of the seas has a separate manager. And likewise regarding the mountains and deserts. And likewise also regarding the cities. For they claimed that each of them has a specific manager from the celestial spirits. And they claimed that plants have a manager, birds have a manager, insects have a manager, and likewise regarding beasts and animals. And these people claimed that the religious communities and religions indicate this meaning. Do you not see in the language of the possessor of the Law, peace be upon him, that he said: 'Jibril is the angel of revelation and knowledge, Mika'il is the angel of provisions, 'Azra'il is the angel of death,' and the angel of mountains is so-and-so, and the angel of seas is so-and-so. Then the practitioners of talismans claimed that it is obligatory upon man to occupy himself with obedience to that spirit, and with its acts of worship, and to take for it a temple, and occupy himself with its worship. And I saw most of the people of India adhering to this doctrine. And it is appropriate to this place that we explain the doctrines of the idol worshippers. So we say: Necessary knowledge is obtained that carved stone and carved wood are not fit for the divinity of the universe. And what is known to be false by intuition (1) is impossible for a great multitude to agree upon for a long time and a prolonged period. And the worship of idols existed before the coming of Noah, peace be upon him, as evidenced by that God Almighty related from the disbelievers of his time their saying: 'Do not abandon your gods, and do not abandon Wadd, nor Suwa', nor Yaghuth, nor Ya'uq, nor Nasr' (1). Then that religion continued from that time in most parts of the earth up to this time. And that indicates that their intention from it is not their belief that the manager of the world is that wood and stone and the image cast in the mold; rather they have interpretations concerning it. The first interpretation—the greatest and strongest—is that the astrologers and practitioners of judgments claimed that the manager of this world is the seven moving planets, because they observed the states of this world linked to the variations of the sun and moon. So they believed in the divinity of these planets. Then they disappear from sight sometimes due to their setting, and sometimes because clouds block their vision, and sometimes because the rest of the planets are hidden due to their falling (2) into the sun's rays. For this reason they took idols in the forms of those planets, and adorned them with things suitable for those planets, then persisted in worshipping them. This is the greatest reason for occupying oneself with idol worship. And what indicates it is that God Almighty, when He related from al-Khalil, peace be upon him, that he said to his father Azar: 'Do you take idols as gods? Indeed, I see you and your people in manifest error' (3). Then after mentioning this speech, he busied himself with establishing the proof that it is not permissible to take the planets, the moon, and the sun as gods. And that is one of the truest proofs that the religion of the idolaters is a branch of this doctrine. The second interpretation: what we have transmitted from India and others—that they said: It is established by induction and by revelation that for every region of the regions of the earth and every group of groups of people there is a celestial spirit that manages them and cares for the improvement of their affairs. And if the matter is so, then it was
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage is an extended exposition by Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, in which he describes the beliefs of the practitioners of talismans and astrologers, and then transitions to explaining the doctrines of idol worshippers, presenting two interpretations. The passage begins with a reference to a previous discussion about the greatest sphere, indicating that the same principle applies to all spheres. Then the author details the talisman practitioners' belief in spirits for each of the 360 degrees, days, hours, and for every division of the earth (seas, mountains, deserts, inhabited areas), as well as for cities, plants, birds, insects, beasts, and animals. They claim that religions support this, citing the Prophet's mention of angels like Jibril, Mika'il, and 'Azra'il as managers. They then claim that humans must worship these spirits and build temples for them. Razi notes that most people of India adhere to this. Then he says it is appropriate to explain the doctrines of idol worshippers. He first argues that necessary knowledge shows carved stone and wood cannot be divine, and it is impossible for a large multitude to agree on something obviously false for a long time. Yet idol worship has existed since before Noah and continues, so there must be interpretations behind it. He presents two interpretations: The first, which he calls the greatest and strongest, is that astrologers observed the influence of the seven planets and believed them to be divine. Since the planets are sometimes hidden (by setting, clouds, or sunlight), they made statues in their forms and worshipped them. Razi cites the story of Abraham arguing against his father's idolatry, showing that the issue was ultimately about the celestial bodies. The second interpretation, from India and elsewhere, is that by induction and revelation, every region and group has a celestial spirit that manages them, and thus they worship statues as representations of these spirits. This interpretation is cut off at the end of the page, leaving the argument incomplete.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Talisman beliefs are just random superstitions without system.
Correction: The passage shows a highly organized cosmic hierarchy with spirits for every domain, backed by selective use of religious texts.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many degrees of the zodiac did talisman practitioners assign spirits to?
A) 360
B) 365
C) 12
D) 7

Key Takeaway
Talisman practitioners believed in an elaborate spirit hierarchy governing all aspects of the cosmos, and they used angelic names from Islam to justify calling for the worship of these spirits.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How often do you find yourself attributing events in your life to 'luck' or 'fate' without acknowledging Allah's sole control? In what specific situation this week can you consciously replace that thought with tawakkul?
?
The talisman practitioners used Islamic angelic names to justify their polytheistic practices. Are there any 'good' habits or Islamic phrases you use that actually veil a subtle reliance on created things rather than Allah? Ask Allah to purify your heart from hidden shirk.
?
If someone today proposed a complex spiritual hierarchy similar to the talisman system but wrapped in Islamic terminology, would you be able to recognize the deviation? What is one practical step you can take to strengthen your knowledge of true tawhid so you are not deceived?

beginner
4 min
Two Interpretations of Idol Worship
Razi presents two interpretations for idol worship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Razi's reasoning that persistent idolatry must have underlying interpretations, and his presentation of two such interpretations: the planetary theory and the regional spirit theory.

Core Idea
Idol worshippers did not worship stone; they worshipped celestial forces through statues.

Al-Razi now turns to explain why idol worship persists despite its obvious falsity. He argues that necessary knowledge proves carved stone cannot be divine, yet the practice has continued since before Noah. Therefore, there must be deeper interpretations. He presents two: first, that idols represent the seven planets which are hidden at times; second, that they represent regional spirits. The first is fully explained; the second is cut short.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Razi's argument for interpretations
Read the introductory argument: necessary knowledge shows stone cannot be divine, but idolatry persists, so there are underlying interpretations.
Note the use of 'necessary knowledge' and 'impossible for a multitude to agree on falsehood'.
2
Study the first interpretation
The astrologers believed the seven planets manage the world and made statues as substitutes when planets are hidden. Note the proof from Abraham's story.
This is called the 'greatest and strongest' interpretation.
3
Note the second interpretation (incomplete)
The second interpretation, from India and others, holds that every region has a celestial spirit, and statues represent them. The passage cuts off here.
Due to page break, the argument is incomplete.

Commentary
This passage is an extended exposition by Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, in which he describes the beliefs of the practitioners of talismans and astrologers, and then transitions to explaining the doctrines of idol worshippers, presenting two interpretations. The passage begins with a reference to a previous discussion about the greatest sphere, indicating that the same principle applies to all spheres. Then the author details the talisman practitioners' belief in spirits for each of the 360 degrees, days, hours, and for every division of the earth (seas, mountains, deserts, inhabited areas), as well as for cities, plants, birds, insects, beasts, and animals. They claim that religions support this, citing the Prophet's mention of angels like Jibril, Mika'il, and 'Azra'il as managers. They then claim that humans must worship these spirits and build temples for them. Razi notes that most people of India adhere to this. Then he says it is appropriate to explain the doctrines of idol worshippers. He first argues that necessary knowledge shows carved stone and wood cannot be divine, and it is impossible for a large multitude to agree on something obviously false for a long time. Yet idol worship has existed since before Noah and continues, so there must be interpretations behind it. He presents two interpretations: The first, which he calls the greatest and strongest, is that astrologers observed the influence of the seven planets and believed them to be divine. Since the planets are sometimes hidden (by setting, clouds, or sunlight), they made statues in their forms and worshipped them. Razi cites the story of Abraham arguing against his father's idolatry, showing that the issue was ultimately about the celestial bodies. The second interpretation, from India and elsewhere, is that by induction and revelation, every region and group has a celestial spirit that manages them, and thus they worship statues as representations of these spirits. This interpretation is cut off at the end of the page, leaving the argument incomplete.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Idol worship is simply ignorance and stupidity without any rationale.
Correction: Al-Razi shows that idol worshippers had elaborate interpretations, such as representing celestial bodies or spirits, which gave their practice internal logic.

Checkpoint
Why does al-Razi use the story of Abraham to support the first interpretation?
A) Abraham worshipped idols himself.
B) Abraham first criticized idol worship and then argued against worshipping celestial bodies, linking the two.
C) Abraham destroyed the idols and then prayed to the planets.
D) Abraham's father was an astrologer.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi argues that persistent idolatry cannot be mere stupidity but stems from interpretations like representing hidden planets or regional spirits.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever considered that idol worship is not simply primitive stupidity, but a misdirected desire for the transcendent? Where in your life do you take a good thing (like ambition, love, or comfort) and treat it as if it were ultimate, forgetting the Creator behind it? What would it take for you to break that habit today?
?
Al-Razi shows that even the disbelievers had some reasoning for their worship. How do you rationalize your own actions that go against divine commands? Are there areas where you have intellectualized your disobedience? Will you stop justifying and start submitting?
?
The idol worshippers made statues because they wanted to worship what they could not see. When you feel distant from Allah, do you create substitutes in your heart—like busyness or entertainment—to fill the gap? What concrete step can you take this week to turn back to the unseen reality of Allah alone?

Celestial Souls and Abstract Intellects: A Comparative View
Definition and comparison of celestial souls and intellects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between celestial souls (attached to bodies) and abstract intellects (disconnected), and their analogy to the human rational soul.

Core Idea
Celestial bodies mirror our souls; some are tied to bodies, others are pure intellects.

In this passage, the author draws a fascinating parallel between the celestial realm and our own human constitution. He introduces two types of celestial entities: those that are like our rational souls in relation to bodies, and those too elevated for any bodily connection. This distinction is foundational for understanding the philosophers' arguments about the unseen world.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the original Arabic and its literal translation to grasp the author's key claims.
2
Identify the two categories
Notice the two types of celestial beings: celestial souls (attached) and abstract intellects (detached).
3
Understand the analogy
Reflect on why the author compares celestial bodies to 'our rational souls in relation to our bodies.' What does that imply?
4
Consider the philosophical context
Recognize that this is part of a larger discussion of proofs for the existence of these entities. The author mentions philosophers have provided detailed proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والكواكب كنفوسنا الناطقة بالنسبة إلى أبداننا وهي المسماة بالنفوس الفلكية ومنها ما هو أعلى شأناً من أن يكون لها تعلق بعالم الأجسام وهي العقول المجردة وقد ذكر دلائل الفلاسفة في إثبات هذه الموجودات على سبيل الاستقصاء.
And the celestial bodies are like our rational souls in relation to our bodies, and they are called the celestial souls. And among them are those that are too elevated to have connection with the world of bodies, and they are the abstract intellects. And he has mentioned the philosophers' proofs for establishing these existents in detail.
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage defines two kinds of celestial entities: celestial souls (attached to bodies) and abstract intellects (disconnected). The author states that philosophers have comprehensively proven their existence. It is a brief definitional passage that sets up a distinction between the two types of celestial beings.

Key Terms
النفوس الفلكية
العقول المجردة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All celestial bodies are themselves intelligent beings without distinction.
Correction: The passage distinguishes between celestial souls (attached to bodies) and abstract intellects (completely detached), showing two different types of intelligent entities.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what are the celestial souls compared to?
A) The abstract intellects
B) Our rational souls in relation to our bodies
C) The philosophers' proofs
D) The world of bodies

Key Takeaway
The passage distinguishes between celestial souls (connected to bodies) and abstract intellects (disconnected), setting the foundation for the philosophers' proofs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your rational soul is like a celestial body directing its sphere. In what areas of your life is your soul leading your body, and where is your body dominating your soul? Commit to one change today to let your soul regain its rightful leadership.
?
The passage describes entities 'too elevated to have connection with the world of bodies.' How attached are you to material comforts? What is one step you can take this week to detach your heart from something worldly and turn toward pure intellect?
?
If you had to classify your own spiritual state right now—are you more like a celestial soul (tied to earthly concerns) or an abstract intellect (focused on higher realities)? What would need to change for you to move upward?
